##### Behavior Creation Mode

You can use the **Behavior Creation Mode** to automatically create an Activity after creating a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024xR3'] in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with Activity diagram' space='MD2024xR3']. The newly created Activity will be set as the behavior of the Call Behavior Action.

To turn on the **Behavior Creation Mode** in an Activity diagram

- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024xR3'], click [IMAGE alt='' src='']. The****Behavior Creation Mode works separatelyfor each project.

When the **Behavior Creation Mode** is on:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024xR3']A Behavior is created together with the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024xR3']. It inherits the type of the Call Behavior Action owner.
- If a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024xR3'] and its [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024xR3'] are not titled, type a name on the Call Behavior Action shape on the diagram, and the typed name will be set as the Behavior's name automatically.

##### Creating Actions by pasting the copied list

You can copy the item list from the text editor (Word, Notepad, etc.), web page, PDF file, PowerPoint slide and paste it in the Activity diagram to create actions.

To create Actions by pasting items from the list

1. Copy the list.
2. Go to the diagram and press Ctrl+V.
3. Select an Action.
4. In the question dialog click Yes if you need to connect the Actions with Control Flow relationship.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Smart layout

###### Dynamiccenterlines

The centerlines are displayed only when the center of the shape that was moved or newly drawn is located near the center of a preexisting shape in the diagram. These lines help you to easily align shapes when drawing a diagram.

When the center of the shape that was moved coincides with a center of any shape that is placed to its right or left, a horizontal centerline appears. When the center of the shape is close to any center of a shape that is located above or below it, a vertical centerline appears.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To switch off the dynamic centerlines

- Click the Show Centerlines button [IMAGE alt='' src=''] in the diagram toolbar, or press C .
- From the Options main menu, select Environment . In the Environment Options dialog, click the Diagram category, and clear the Show Centerlines in Flow Diagrams check box in the Display properties group.

###### Diagram orientation

The diagram orientation is used to assign the correct rectilinear path breaks and draw paths between the Activity diagram shapes. The paths can be drawn from side to side, or from the lower to the upper shape borders.

#### TIP: Example

Example

If you have a vertical diagram orientation and shapes are not in the same centerline, the paths will be connected from the lower border of the first shape to the upper border of the next shape, adding break points: 
[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
If you have a horizontal diagram orientation, the paths will be connected from the side border of the first shape to the next side border of the second shape, adding breakpoints: 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To change the diagram orientation

- From the Options main menu, select Project . In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Setting project options' space='MD2024xR3']**Project Options** dialog , expand Symbol Styles > Default > Diagram group (if it is not expanded by default) and, in the options list, change the value for the Diagram Orientation property.
- From the diagram pane shortcut menu, select Diagram Properties, or press Shift+Enter to open the Diagram Properties dialog. Change the value for the Diagram Orientation property in that dialog.

##### Deleting from Activity diagrams

- Note that after deleting the last symbol of an element from the Activity diagram, the element will be automatically removed from the model. This does not affect [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Pin' space='MD2024xR3'] and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activity Parameter Node' space='MD2024xR3'] .
- If a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Call Behavior Action' space='MD2024xR3'] that has an assigned [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024xR3'] is deleted from the Activity diagram, then this Behavior is also deleted from the model.

This is valid if the assigned Behavior is editable and does not have more usages, i.e. there is not a Call Behavior Action that has a reference to this Behavior.

##### Displaying inner elements

To display inner elements

- When creating a new Activity diagram, right-click an Activity in the Containment tree, click Create Diagram , and then click Activity Diagram .

Inner elements are displayed on the Activity diagram pane automatically upon creating the first diagram under the Activity element.

- When modifying a previously created Activity diagram, select the diagram pane and do one of the following:

- From the shortcut menu, click**Display**>**Display Inner Elements**. 
- On the diagram toolbar click[IMAGE alt='' src=''],and select**Display Inner Elements**.

<strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> to automatically create an Activity after creating a <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link> in the <ac:link><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Activity Diagram]]></ac:plain-text-link-body><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link>. The newly created Activity will be set as the behavior of the Call Behavior Action.</p><p>To turn on the <strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> in an Activity diagram</p><hr /><ul><li><p class="auto-cursor-target">In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram palette]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>, click <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image ac:title="Behavior Creation Mode" ac:alt="Behavior Creation Mode"><ri:attachment ri:filename="automatic_behavior_creation.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span>.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="8a792f8e-361c-4f23-8d0f-6accbb0243b6"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span><span class="confluence-link">The<strong> </strong>Behavior Creation Mode works <span><span class="confluence-link">separately </span></span>for each project.</span></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ul><p>When the <strong>Behavior Creation Mode</strong> is on:</p><ul><li><span><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Behavior" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:link-body><span style="color: rgb(0,51,102);">A</span> Behavior</ac:link-body></ac:link> is created together with the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link>. It inherits the type of the Call Behavior Action owner.</span></li><li>If a <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link> and its <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Behavior" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link> are not titled, type a name on the Call Behavior Action shape on the diagram, and the typed name will be set as the Behavior's name automatically.</li></ul><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Creating Actions by pasting the copied list</h3><p><span style="color: rgb(62,63,64);">You can copy the item list from the text editor (Word, Notepad, etc.), web page, PDF file, PowerPoint slide and paste it in the Activity diagram to create actions.</span></p><p><br /></p><p>To create Actions by pasting items from the list</p><hr /><ol><li>Copy the list.</li><li>Go to the diagram and press Ctrl+V.</li><li>Select an Action.</li><li>In the question dialog click <strong>Yes</strong> if you need to connect the Actions with Control Flow relationship.</li></ol><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="paste_list_to_create_activities.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Smart layout</h3><h4><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">Dynamic</span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);"> </span>centerlines</h4><p>The centerlines are displayed only when the center of the shape that was moved or newly drawn is located near the center of a preexisting shape in the diagram. These lines help you to easily align shapes when drawing a diagram.</p><p>When the center of the shape that was moved coincides with a center of any shape that is placed to its right or left, a horizontal centerline appears. When the center of the shape is close to any center of a shape that is located above or below it, a vertical centerline appears.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /> <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image ac:alt="Dynamic vertical centerline"><ri:attachment ri:filename="dynamic_centerline_vertical.gif"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p><p>To switch off the dynamic centerlines</p><hr /><ul><li>Click the <strong>Show Centerlines</strong> button <span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="show_centerlines.gif"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span> in the diagram toolbar, or press <strong>C</strong>.</li><li>From the <strong>Options</strong> main menu, select <strong>Environment</strong>. In the<strong> Environment Options</strong> dialog, click the <strong>Diagram</strong> category, and clear the <strong>Show Centerlines in Flow Diagrams</strong> check box in the <strong>Display</strong> properties group.</li></ul><p><br /></p><h4>Diagram orientation</h4><p>The diagram orientation is used to assign the correct rectilinear path breaks and draw paths between the Activity diagram shapes. The paths can be drawn from side to side, or from the lower to the upper shape borders.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="tip" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c7b66ba1-861d-466b-a5e1-a9b825bb1752"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Example</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p> If you have a vertical diagram orientation and shapes are not in the same centerline, the paths will be connected from the lower border of the first shape to the upper border of the next shape, adding break points: <br class="atl-forced-newline" /><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="diagram_orientation_vertical.gif"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />If you have a horizontal diagram orientation, the paths will be connected from the side border of the first shape to the next side border of the second shape, adding breakpoints: <br class="atl-forced-newline" /><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="diagram_orientation_horizontal.gif"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper">To change the diagram orientation</span></p><hr /><ul><li>From the <strong>Options</strong> main menu, select <strong>Project</strong>. In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Setting project options" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:link-body><strong>Project Options</strong> dialog</ac:link-body></ac:link>, expand <strong>Symbol Styles </strong>&gt;<strong> Default </strong>&gt;<strong> </strong><strong>Diagram</strong> group (if it is not expanded by default) and, in the options list, change the value for the <strong>Diagram Orientation</strong> property.</li><li>From the diagram pane shortcut menu, select <strong>Diagram Properties,</strong> or press Shift+Enter to open the <strong>Diagram Properties</strong> dialog. Change the value for the <strong>Diagram Orientation</strong> property in that dialog.</li></ul><h3 class="with-breadcrumbs">Deleting from Activity diagrams</h3><ul><li>Note that after deleting the last symbol of an element from the Activity diagram, the element will be automatically removed from the model. This does not affect <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Pin" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Pins]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> and <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Activity Parameter Node" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Activity Parameter Nodes]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</li><li><p>If a <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Call Behavior Action" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link> that has an assigned <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Behavior" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link> is deleted from the Activity diagram, then this Behavior is also deleted from the model.</p></li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d276b872-4811-4d21-98eb-dcfc6695d559"><ac:rich-text-body><p><span>This is valid if the assigned Behavior is editable and does not have more usages, i.e. there is not a Call Behavior Action that has a reference to this Behavior.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Displaying inner elements</h3><p>To display inner elements</p><hr /><ul><li>When creating a new Activity diagram, right-click an Activity in the Containment tree, click <strong>Create Diagram</strong>, and then click <strong>Activity</strong><strong> </strong><strong>Diagram</strong>.</li></ul><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="43ea6a6d-d91c-48af-8008-72e4437c353a"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Inner elements are displayed on the Activity diagram pane automatically upon creating the first diagram under the Activity element.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ul><li><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper">When modifying a previously created Activity diagram, select the diagram pane and do one of the following:<br /></span></li></ul><p style="margin-left: 30.0px;"><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><span>- From the shortcut menu, click </span><strong>Display</strong><span> &gt;</span><strong> Display Inner Elements</strong><span>.</span><br /><span>- On the diagram toolbar click </span><span class="confluence-embedded-file-wrapper"><ac:image ac:title="Display" ac:alt="Display"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Display.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Activity diagram" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image>,</span><span> and select</span><strong> Display Inner Elements</strong><span>.</span><br /></span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150197 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01247: Working with Associations

- page_id: `227150197`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150197/Working+with+Associations
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-11-14T09:11:23.987+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Association
- labels: ['reflective-association', 'association-class']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1018698642

1018698644

1018698643

An [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Association' space='MD2024xR3'] is a relationship between two classes. It is represented by a solid line. Though associations are bi-directional by default, they can also be unidirectional, where one class knows about the other class and the relationship but the other class does not. Sometimes an association links a class to itself. This association is called a recursive (reflexive) association. One example of this association is an employee who is managed by a manager who is also himself an employee.

To draw a recursive (reflexive) association

1. Select Association .
2. Click a class ( Employee in this example) and hover over the class until you see a rectangle shape. Click the class again to create a recursive association. [ATTACHMENT filename='recursiveAssociation.png']

##### Association Properties

You can specify association properties in the association [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3']. The description of each property appears in the same window. The description area of the Specification window presents the descriptions.

To show the direction arrow near the association name

1. Do one of the following:
  - Right-click the association, and from the shortcut menu, select Show Direction Arrow .
  - Open the association [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Symbol Properties dialog' space='MD2024xR3'] dialog and set the Show Direction Arrow property to true .

The default Direction Arrow direction is displayed according to the path creation direction.

To change the **Direction Arrow** direction

1. Right-click the association.
2. From the shortcut menu, select Reverse Direction Arrow .

The Direction Arrow is a graphical representation most often used in top-level domain class diagrams. It helps to read a diagram and explains diagram semantics, and has no meaning in a model.

Usually, you would use the Direction Arrow on a diagram where navigability is not yet defined. Direction Arrows are usually displayed for named associations. When you create more detailed diagrams with specified navigability, direction arrows and association names are not usually displayed in these types of diagrams.

As shown in the following figure, *User* and *Account* Classes are connected with the Association. A navigation arrow can be displayed on either side depending on the Association name. If the association name is *belongs to*, the Direction Arrow should point from the *Account* to the *User*. If the Association name is *has*, the Direction Arrow should point from the *User* to the *Account*.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Examples of Direction Arrows

In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class diagram' space='MD2024xR3'], you can add [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Attribute' space='MD2024xR3'] to an Association using an [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Association Class' space='MD2024xR3']. The Association Class is a simple [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class' space='MD2024xR3']with a dashed line connected to the Association.

##### Adding Association between Read-Only Classifiers

Adding a new Association always creates two roles or properties at both ends. They are owned by the attached Classifier by default. However, when one or both ends of the Association are not editable (for example, locked in a server project or stored in a read-only profile or used project), the properties will be ownedby the Association itself. In this case, a warning appears informing you about any unexpected issue in model creation.

1018698641

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3'] [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227148742 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01248: Working with attached files

- page_id: `227148742`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148742/Working+with+attached+files
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:24.278+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects > Projects with file attachments
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

The actions you can perform with attached files are listed below:

Attached files can also be included in reports. The attached file is saved in the file system together with the generated report. In this report, any hyperlink to that attached file defined in the model is replaced with reference to the appropriate file in the file system.

##### Modifying the contents

Attached files can be opened directly from the modeling tool and reviewed or modified with appropriate programs (documents – with MS Word, worksheets – with MS Excel, HTML files – with any HTML editor).

To open an attached file, do one of the following

- In the Containment tree, double-click the attached file.
- In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select Open File .
- Double-click either the element that has an active hyperlink to the attached file, or the shape of that element (see the following figure).

The file is opened in the appropriate program in your operating system. You can review or modify it.

[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
 
After closing the modified file, you can choose whether to save it in the modeling tool or not. Saving the latest version of the file in the modeling tool updates the **Modified** **At** property value of the appropriate Attached File element.

If the attached file is read-only, the changes made to it cannot be saved. To allow modifying the file, do one of the following:

- If the file is attached to used project, change the accessibility mode of this used project from read-only to read-write .
- If the file is attached to server project, lock the Attached File element for edit.

##### Inserting into HTML text

Attached image files can be inserted into HTML texts and displayed on diagrams. 
 
To insert an attached image file into HTML text

1. In the Containment tree, right-click the attached image file and select Copy Image URL .
2. On a diagram pane, draw a text box with the HTML mode on.
3. [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Advanced HTML Editor dialog' space='MD2024xR3']Open the **Advanced HTML Editor** dialog .
4. On the toolbar, click the Insert image button and select either:
  - From File button, then paste the URL into the Picture source field.
  - **From Attached File**button, then find and select the attached image file in the list. If you are working with a server project, make sure that the path to the image location is accessible from any computer that has Internet connection. Otherwise, the image won't be displayed, when the project is opened on another computer.
5. Click OK twice to close both the Picture Properties and Advanced HTML Editor dialogs.

The inserted image appears on the diagram. Now if you transfer the project to another computer, the diagram continues displaying the image. You can also insert images that are not yet attached to the project model. Read more about [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Inserting images into HTML text' space='MD2024xR3'][.](http://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Inserting+an+image+into+HTML+text)

##### Exporting back to the local file system

To export the attached file back to the local file system

1. In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select**Save File As** .
2. Select the location in the local file system and click **Save**.

The file is saved in the local file system.

##### Creating image shapes

You can use attached imagefiles (*.gif*, *.jpg*, *.jpeg*, *.svg*, or *.png*) to create image shapes on the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024xR3'].

To create an image shape using an attached image file

1. In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Containment tab' space='MD2024xR3'] select an already attached file or attach a new one. [How to attach a file in the Containment tree >>](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Attaching%252C+reattaching%252C+and+detaching+files#Attaching,reattaching,anddetachingfiles-Attachingfiles) Image formatsYou can attach images of the following formats: *.gif*, *.jpg*, *.jpeg*, *.svg*, or *.png*.
2. Drag the attached file element to the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024xR3'].The image shape is created. Image does not updateImage shape is not synchronized with attached file. If you replace an image in the attached file, the image shape on the diagram pane will not update.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>The actions you can perform with attached files are listed below:</p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="toc" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="ff2ea14a-5e49-4318-87a0-9ad533580594" />    </p><p>Attached files can also be included in reports. The attached file is saved in the file system together with the generated report. In this report, any hyperlink to that attached file defined in the model is replaced with reference to the appropriate file in the file system.</p><h3>Modifying the contents</h3><p>Attached files can be opened directly from the modeling tool and reviewed or modified with appropriate programs (documents – with MS Word, worksheets – with MS Excel, HTML files – with any HTML editor).</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" />To open an attached file, do one of the following</p><hr /><ul><li>In the Containment tree, double-click the attached file.</li><li>In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select <strong>Open File</strong>.</li><li>Double-click either the element that has an active hyperlink to the attached file, or the shape of that element (see the following figure).</li></ul><p>The file is opened in the appropriate program in your operating system. You can review or modify it.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><ac:image ac:border="true" ac:title="Element (left) and its shape (right) with active hyperlink to the attached file" ac:alt="Element (left) and its shape (right) with active hyperlink to the attached file" ac:height="68" ac:width="454"><ri:attachment ri:filename="active_hyperlink_to_attached_file.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with attached files" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image><br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />After closing the modified file, you can choose whether to save it in the modeling tool or not. Saving the latest version of the file in the modeling tool updates the <strong>Modified</strong> <strong>At</strong> property value of the appropriate Attached File element.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="05c871af-43a3-44e4-a88e-0ccb95217dcc"><ac:rich-text-body><p>If the attached file is read-only, the changes made to it cannot be saved. To allow modifying the file, do one of the following:</p><ul><li>If the file is attached to used project, change the accessibility mode of this used project from <em>read-only</em> to <em>read-write</em>.</li><li>If the file is attached to server project, lock the Attached File element for edit.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Inserting into HTML text</h3><p>Attached image files can be inserted into HTML texts and displayed on diagrams.<br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />To insert an attached image file into HTML text</p><hr /><ol><li>In the Containment tree, right-click the attached image file and select <strong>Copy Image URL</strong>.</li><li>On a diagram pane, draw a text box with the HTML mode on.</li><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Advanced HTML Editor dialog" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:link-body>Open the <strong>Advanced HTML Editor</strong> dialog</ac:link-body></ac:link>.</li><li>On the toolbar, click the <strong>Insert image</strong> button and select either:<br /><br /><ul><li><strong>From File</strong> button, then paste the URL into the <strong>Picture source</strong> field.</li><li><p><strong>From Attached File </strong>button, then find and select the attached image file in the list.<br /><br /></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="2d581ff2-2ef7-4a34-923b-c4475947f5df"><ac:rich-text-body><p>If you are working with a server project, make sure that the path to the image location is accessible from any computer that has Internet connection. Otherwise, the image won't be displayed, when the project is opened on another computer.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li></ul></li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong> twice to close both the <strong>Picture Properties</strong> and <strong>Advanced HTML Editor</strong> dialogs.</li></ol><p>The inserted image appears on the diagram. Now if you transfer the project to another computer, the diagram continues displaying the image. You can also insert images that are not yet attached to the project model. Read more about <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Inserting images into HTML text" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link><a href="http://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Inserting+an+image+into+HTML+text" style="letter-spacing: 0.0px;">.</a></p><h3>Exporting back to the local file system</h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To export the attached file back to the local file system</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the Containment tree, right-click the attached file and select<strong> Save File As</strong></span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Select the location in the local file system and click <strong>Save</strong>.</span></li></ol><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The file is saved in the local file system.</span></p><h3><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">Creating image shapes</span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">You can use attached <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">image </span>files (<em>.gif</em>, <em>.jpg</em>, <em>.jpeg</em>, <em>.svg</em>, or <em>.png</em>) to create image shapes on the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram pane]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>.</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create an image shape using an attached image file<br /></span></p><hr /><ol><li><p class="auto-cursor-target"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Containment tab" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[Containment tree]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> select an already attached file or attach a new one. <a href="https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Attaching%252C+reattaching%252C+and+detaching+files#Attaching,reattaching,anddetachingfiles-Attachingfiles">How to attach a file in the Containment tree &gt;&gt;</a><br /></span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="b358091b-36ab-4b19-bf3e-c86561895db6"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Image formats</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">You can attach images of the following formats: <em>.gif</em>, <em>.jpg</em>, <em>.jpeg</em>, <em>.svg</em>, or <em>.png</em>.</span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li><li><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Drag the attached file element to the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[diagram pane]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>. </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The image shape is created.</span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="81c9aecf-0a06-41e4-8c81-c3974cbc5eef"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Image does not update</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>Image shape is not synchronized with <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">attached file. If you replace an image in the attached file, the image shape on the diagram pane will not update. </span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p></li></ol>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227151417 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01249: Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard

- page_id: `227151417`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227151417/Working+with+Automatic+Instantiation+Wizard
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:51.470+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Tools > Automatic Instantiation Wizard
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Note

907302760

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Note

907302781

907302758

**On this page**

3

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Note

907302771

You can create several different sets of instances using the **Automatic Instantiation** wizard. You can add each set to a different package and display it on a newly created diagram.

Depending on the size of your system, a very large number of instance specifications can be created using the wizard. That is why we strongly recommend selecting a new package wherein all created instance specifications will be stored.

##### Step #1. Selecting parts to be instantiated

In this step, you can see all the available instance specification values (parts) of your selected element. At this point, you can select which parts or properties to instantiate, create or select values for parts and properties, as well as add or remove parallel parts.

You can select/deselect the parts by clicking the check marks next to the parts or the options in the Selection area.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Parts are displayed if the multiplicity is greater than 1. The number of parts displayed depends on the multiplicity.

- If the multiplicity is a particular value, for example 2, then you will see 2 parts displayed in the **Automatic Instantiation**wizard. Also, in this case, you will not be able to add parallel parts or remove existing parallel parts.
- If the multiplicity is defined as an interval (for example, 0..*, 1..10, 1..* ) or *, only one part will be created by default. If you need more parts, you can create them by pressing **Insert** or selecting **Add parallel part** from the selected property’s shortcut menu.
- If the multiplicity is 1, parts will not be created.

The parts and properties are displayed with the suggested types, names, and values. In this step of the wizard, you can change them. You can also change the type for the part only if there is an available sub-element for that part in your model (see the Case study).

**Selecting a value for an instance**

To select a value for an instance

1. Select a part to be instantiated to which you want to add a value.
2. In **Instantiated properties**, click a **Value** specification cell and then click the ... button.
3. The **Select Instance Specification** dialog opens.
4. In the opened dialog, select the instance specification you want to add for the selected instance.
5. Click the **OK** button.

To create a value for an instance

1. Select a part to be instantiated for which you want to create a value.
2. In **Instantiated properties**, click the **Value** specification cell and then click the **Show Shortcut Menu** button. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. In the opened shortcut menu, point to the **Value Specification** and then select one of the available value types.
4. In the **Value property** specification cell, type the desired value. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

**Changing the name of an instance**

Each instance has a defaultname that uses the dot notation. However, you can change the default name by clicking the value row next to the **Name** property and typing the new name for the instance. ****

[IMAGE alt='' src=''] ****

**Applying a custom stereotypeto an instance**

You can also apply the custom stereotype to the instance. Only those stereotypes can be applied that have *Instance Specification* as their metaclass and whose customizations have a meta property named *classifier*with the **New Types** property value set to the instantiated element’s type.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The custom «ControllerFMU» and «ControllerSTM» stereotypes have *Instance Specification* as their metaclass 
and their respective customizations *ControllerFMU Customization* and *ControllerSTM Customization* have a meta property named classifier with the **New Types** property value set to the «Controller» stereotype. 
Since the *Controller* class has the «Controller» stereotype applied, the «ControllerFMU» and «ControllerSTM» stereotypes can be applied to the *Controller* class's instance.

**Changing a type for an instance**

You can change the type for the property's instance only if that type is a subtype of a Class (connected throughGeneralization). As shown in the following figure, the *Engine GM* Class and *Engine GMR C*lass are subtypes of the *Engine*Class. When creating an instance for the *Vehicle* Class, you can change the type of the *engine*Property by selecting one of the following: *Engine GM* Class, *Engine GMR* Class, or *Engine*Class.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Changing the type for a Part Property instance directly in the Automatic Instantiation dialog.

##### Step #2. Selecting a package

In this step, you can select the package to store instance specifications. You can select anexisting package from the element tree, create a new package, or clone selectedpackages. Click the **Finish** buttonafter this step if you do not want to display your created instance specifications.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To create a new Package in the element tree

1. In the element tree, select the Package for which you want to create the new one.
2. Click the **Creation Mode** button.
3. Click the **Create Owner** button.
4. From the open menu, select the package kind. The Specification window of that package opens.
5. Type its name.
6. Click **Close**.

To clone the Packages in the element tree

1. In the element tree, select the Package to clone. The Package is cloned recursively including all nested structures.
2. Click the **Clone** button.
3. The Specification window of cloned Package opens.
4. Type its name.
5. Click **Close**.

##### Step #3. Creating a diagram (optional)

In this step, you can choose whether you want to show your created instance specifications in a new diagram or not. If you do not wish to create a new diagram, you can simply skip this step.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To create a diagram using **Automatic Instantiation** Wizard

1. If you choose to create a new diagram for displaying instance specification(s), select the **Create a new diagram**check box.
2. If you wish to create and display links between your instance specification(s), select the **Create link between instances**check box.
3. Fill in the **Type diagram name**field by typing the diagram name. NoteBy default, the diagram name is the selected Package's name in Step 2.
4. From the **Select diagram type** drop-down list, you can select one of the diagram types.
5. Specify the owner for a new diagram:
  - Select existing Packages from the tree.
  - Click the **Create Owner** button to create a new one.
  - Click the **Clone** button to clone existing Packages.
6. After clicking the **Finish** button, a new diagram with instance specifications is created and displayed in your project.

907308985

When creating an instance for the <em>Vehicle</em> Class, you can change the type of the <em>engine </em>Property by selecting one of the following: <em>Engine GM</em> <span> Class, <em>Engine GMR</em> </span> <span> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Class</span>, or <em>Engine </em><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Class</span></span><span>.</span> </span></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="specifying_type_for_instantiated_properties.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;margin-bottom: 20.0px;"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Changing the type for a Part Property instance directly in the Automatic Instantiation dialog.</span></h6><h3><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Step #2. <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Selecting a package</span> </span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In this step, you can select the package to store instance specifications. You can select an </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">existing package from the element tree, create a new package, or clone selected </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">packages.</span> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Finish</strong> button </span><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">after this step if you do not want to display your created instance specifications.</span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="select_package_step2.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <br /> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create a new Package in the element tree</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the element tree, select the Package for which you want to create the new one.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Creation Mode</strong> button. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Create Owner</strong> button.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">From the open menu, select the package kind. The Specification window of that package opens.<br /> </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Type its name.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</span></li></ol><p><br /></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To clone the Packages <span>in the element tree</span> </span></p><hr /><ol><li><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In the element tree, select the Package to clone.<br /> </span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="eeb6f4cf-5cbe-45ab-9321-bf829e0ba307"><ac:rich-text-body>The Package is cloned recursively including all nested structures.</ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Clone</strong> button.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">The Specification window of cloned Package opens.<br /> </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Type its name.</span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click <strong>Close</strong>.</span></li></ol><h3><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Step #3. <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Creating a diagram (optional)</span> </span></h3><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">In this step, you can choose whether you want to show your created instance specifications in a new diagram or not. If you do not wish to create a new diagram, you can simply skip this step.</span></p><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="create_diagram_step3.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Automatic Instantiation Wizard" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <br /> </span></p><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">To create a diagram using <strong>Automatic Instantiation</strong> Wizard</span></p><hr /><ol><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">If you choose to create a new diagram for displaying instance specification(s), select the <strong>Create a new diagram </strong><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">check box</span>. </span></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">If you wish to create and display links between your instance specification(s), <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">select the </span> <strong>Create link between instances </strong>check box.</span></li><li><p class="auto-cursor-target"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Fill in the </span> <strong>Type diagram name </strong><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">field by typing the diagram name.<br /> </span> </span> </span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="4db12659-8cdc-4979-b226-9ee2bb0450af"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Note</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> By default, the diagram name is the selected Package's name in Step 2.<br /> </span></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">From the <strong>Select diagram type</strong> drop-down list, you can select one of the diagram types.</span></li><li>Specify the owner for a new diagram:<ul><li>Select existing Packages from the tree.</li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);"> <span>Click the <strong>Create Owner </strong></span></span>button to create a new one.</li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">Click the <strong>Clone</strong> button to clone existing Packages.</span></li></ul></li><li><span style="color: rgb(51,51,51);">After clicking the <strong>Finish</strong> button, a new diagram with instance specifications is created and displayed in your project. </span></li></ol></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="efee3e9e-7b4f-43e7-8821-e2cdc94040d0"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">907308985</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><ul><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Automatic Instantiation Wizard Case Study" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link></li><li class="with-breadcrumbs"><ac:link><ri:page ri:space-key="SYSMLP2024xR3" ri:content-title="Automatic Instantiation wizard" /><ac:link-body><span class="current">Automatic Instantiation wizard</span> in SysML Plugin</ac:link-body></ac:link></li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro>

## PAGE 01250: Working with cells

- page_id: `227149516`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149516/Working+with+cells
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-07-08T07:25:35.344+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > Tables > Basic tasks in tables
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Data types

1343270176

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Data types

1343270178

1343270175

**On this page**

43

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Data types

1343270177

This section explains how to work with cells in the table: selection, entering and clearing values, opening an element's Specification window, and navigation.

##### selectingSelecting cells

In all tables, you can select:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']
- Multiple cells.[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']
- Entire table.[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']

singleTo select a single cell

1. Press the left mouse button on the table.

multipleTo select multiple cells, do one of the following

- Press the left mouse button and drag a mouse pointer.
- Press Shift and use the left mouse button or any of the arrow keys from the keyboard.

entireTo select an entire table

1. Right-click the column # header.
2. From the shortcut menu, select the Select command. [ATTACHMENT filename='select_table.png']

##### Entering values into a cell

Individual cells in the table cannot be edited if the text is highlighted in grey. This means the cell contains a predefined value and is non-editable.

All changes made in the table are saved in the model. The procedure below describes how to enter a value into an editable cell.

To enter a value into a cell

1. Double-click a cell you want to edit.
2. One of the following actions is available, depending on the property type of the column in which the selected cell is found: - Type the value directly in the selected cell. - Click the Edit button. The [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3'] opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='gt_edit_cell.png'] - Click the Add (+) to specify a value. - Select the value from the drop down list.
3. In the opened property value editor specify required properties. The value is saved in the model.

##### Opening the Specification window of an element from a cell

The property can be edited in the element’s [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] if it is not locked.

To open the element’s [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] from a cell

Do either:

- If the cell is non-editable, double-click it.
- If the cell is editable, right-click on a cell, and from the shortcut menu select Specification. Then: [ATTACHMENT filename='gt_open_specification_submenu.png']
  - If the selected cell does not refer to any element, the Specification window of the element in the row will open.
  - If the selected cell refers to more than one element, the submenu with the list of appropriate elements will open. Choose the element whose [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] you want to open.

##### Clearing values from cells

You can clear values from a single or multiple cells in cells containing the following data types: String, Boolean, Number, or Enumeration. You can clear the whole table, column, or row.

#### WARNING: Data types

Data types

Only String, Boolean, Number, or Enumeration data types can be cleared from a cell.

The procedures below describe how to clear values from individual cells, from a block of cells, or from the entire table:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']

clear from cellsTo clear values from cells

1. Select single or multiple cells in the table. ]]>[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']
2. Do one of the following: Selected cells of String, Boolean, Number, or Enumeration data types become empty. The following example demonstrates that the Documentation cell is empty after clearing because its data type is a String. The Is Abstract cell value also is cleared because the value type is Boolean. [ATTACHMENT filename='cleared_cells.png']
  - From the shortcut menu, select the Clear command (see the following figure).
  - Press Delete from keyboard (see the following figure). [ATTACHMENT filename='clear_cell.png']

clear from tableTo clear values from an entire table

1. Select the entire table. ]]>[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with cells' space='MD2024xR3']
2. Do one of the following: - From the table shortcut menu, click the Clear command. - Press Delete on the keyboard.

##### Navigation between cells

Navigate between cells using the arrow keys from the keyboard and keyboard shortcuts.

| Press | To move... |
| --- | --- |
| Right Arrow key | One cell to the right. |
| Left Arrow key | One cell to the left. |
| Down Arrow key | One cell down. |
| Up Arrow key | One cell up. |
| Tab | One cell to the right. |
| Shift+Tab | To the previous cell. |
| Enter | To the cell below. |
| Shift+Enter | To the cell above. |

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150218 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01251: Working with Classes

- page_id: `227150218`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150218/Working+with+Classes
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-11-14T12:02:48.067+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Class
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: More Information

1408655808

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: More Information

1408655819

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: More Information

1408655809

A [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class' space='MD2024xR3'] can be defined as active (a border to the Class shape is added). An active Class specifies whether an object of the Class maintains its own thread of control.

General information about working with shapes is provided in [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Diagramming' space='MD2024xR3'].

You can specify Class properties in the Class's Specification window. In the same window, you can find the description of each property. Descriptions are presented in the description area at the bottom of the Specification window.

#### TIP: More information

More information

- For more information about the Specification window, see the page [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] .
- For more information about specifying property values, see the page [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3'] .

To insert an inner element in the selected class

1. Double-click the selected Class or select Specification from the Class's [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Shortcut menu' space='CDH185'] . The Class's Specification window opens.
2. Click the Inner Elements tab and then click the Create button or press Insert .
3. Select the element you wish to add from the list. Click the selected element.
4. The corresponding Specification window opens. Define the Class, Use Case, or Interface, and click OK . [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-09 at 12.30.14 AM.png']

To generate operations for setting or getting private data to the selected class

- From the Class's shortcut menu, select Tools and then Create Setters/Getters . [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-09 at 12.32.54 AM.png']

#### TIP: More Information

More Information

For a detailed description, read [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating Setters and Getters' space='MD2024xR3'].

To control a list of operations and attributes that are visible on a diagram

1. Select Edit Compartmen t from the Class's shortcut menu.
2. The Compartment Edit dialog opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-09 at 12.39.07 AM.png']

To define a class as abstract and/or active

1. Open the Class's Specification window.
2. In the General tab, select the Is Abstract , and/or Is Active check box to true .

To show members (attributes and operations) on the classifier shape according to the visibility

1. On the diagram pane, right-click the Class shape and then from the class's shortcut menu, select the Symbol Properties .
2. In the Symbol Properties dialog, change the Show Members property; the options are All, Only Public, or Not Private.

1408655807

**Related references**

true[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class' space='MD2024xR3']

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class Diagram Wizard' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Behavior' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227149522 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01252: Working with columns

- page_id: `227149522`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149522/Working+with+columns
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-07-08T08:28:36.706+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > Tables > Basic tasks in tables
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Additional information

1344888677

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Additional information

1344888679

1344888676

**On this page**

43

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Additional information

1344888678

This section shows how to work with columns in the table: selection, clearing values, hiding, reordering, adding, and removing columns.

##### Selecting an entire column

To select an entire column

1. Right-click the column header.
2. From the shortcut menu, click the Select command.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Clearing values from an entire column

#### WARNING: Data types

Data types

Only String, Boolean, Number, or Enumeration data types can be cleared from a cell.

To clear values from an entire column

1. Right-click the column header.
2. Do one of the following: - From the shortcut menu, click the Clear command. - Press Delete from the keyboard.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Hiding a column

To hide a column

1. Select single or multiple cells, and from the shortcut menu, select Column > Hide .
2. Right-click the column header to open the shortcut menu, and select the Hide command.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Reordering columns

To reorder columns

- Click the column header and drag it to the desired place. Only the first column cannot be moved.

##### Adding and removing columns

To add or remove columns

1. To open the available columns list: Using the **Select Columns** dialog, you can choose to display the properties of the specified element type, as well as the properties that are subtypes of the specified element type.
  - On the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Table toolbars' space='MD2024xR3'] , click the Columns to open the menu with common properties corresponding to element types that have been selected for the table.
  - On the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Table toolbars' space='MD2024xR3'] , click Columns > Select Columns to open the dialog with all properties, including tags of stereotypes corresponding to selected element types.
2. Do one of the following:

- 
  - Select the properties you want to see as columns in the table.
  - Unselect the properties you do not want to see as columns in the table.

##### Adding and removing Custom Columns

Custom Columns allow you to create structured expressions the results of which are only visible in the table for which the Custom Column is created. If you prefer to create an expression that can be reusable in multiple tables, matrices, maps, and other locations where structured expressions are accepted, you need to [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Custom traceability rules' space='MD2024xR3'] instead.

To add Custom Columns

1. In the toolbar, click **Show Columns**/**Columns** > **New Custom Column**. 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']
2. In the **Expression** dialog, specify criteria for the Custom Column, and click **OK**.

To remove Custom Columns

1. Right-click the Custom Column header you want to remove.
2. From the shortcut menu, select the Remove Custom Column command. [ATTACHMENT filename='remove_custom_column.png']

##### Specifying Custom Columns

When you create a new Custom Column, you need to define the expression in the **Expression** dialog. Keep in mind:

- The Custom Column type and multiplicity (conveyed via the Single Value check box) are set automatically according to the specified expression once it is created or edited. You can also change them manually, however, they will only be applied if you make no modifications to the expression itself. [ATTACHMENT filename='derived_property_type_and_multiplicity_img.png']
- The root union of a Custom Column structured expression has the Unique check box which you can select to have only one identical element count as the result displayed in the table column cell. By default, the check box is selected. [ATTACHMENT filename='unique_ordered_options.png']

#### INFO: Additional information

Additional information

- To learn more about specifying expressions, see the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specifying criteria for querying model' space='MD2024xR3'] page.
- You can also select to show implied relationships in the table. The procedure for specifying which relationships to display in the table is the same as described in [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Selecting criteria' space='MD2024xR3'] .

##### Editing Custom Columns

To edit a Custom Column

1. In a table, right-click the header of the desired Custom Column and select Edit Custom Column .
2. In the Expression dialog, make desired changes and click OK .

##### Setting detailed column names

Column names in the table header are set automatically. They are element property names. You cannot change column names. If an element has some properties with the same name (for example, in associations or if a tag of stereotypes is selected as a column), detailed column names could provide more precise information.

To see detailed column names

- On the Options toolbar, click [ATTACHMENT filename='options_button.png'] and then select Show Detailed Column Name . The group name (between brackets) to which the selected property belongs, and/or the stereotype name (just before the property name), will be displayed in the column heading.

The following diagram shows three different columns with the same name for the association element: **Name**, **Name** (Role of A), and **Name** (Role of B), and a column for the class element with the stereotype «Teacher». **Name** (Tags). If the command **Show Detailed Column Name** were not selected, there would be four columns with the same headings, i.e., **Name**.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150285 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01253: Working with Constraints

- page_id: `227150285`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150285/Working+with+Constraints
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-12-19T13:31:03.734+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Constraint
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can edit constraints in the **Constraints** property group of the containing element Specification window, in the constraint’s Specification window, or double click the selected constraint and edit it on the diagram pane directly.

To see the constraint expression, make sure the **Show Constraint** value is set to true, in the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Symbol Properties dialog' space='MD2024xR3']**Symbol Properties** dialog.

In this section, see the following procedures:

##### Defining a new constraint

To define a new constraint, do one of the following

- In the Containment Tree, from the element shortcut menu, select Create Element > Constraint .
- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] , select the Inner Elements property group and click the Create button (select Constraint from the list, if needed). Specify the constraint in the constraint [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] .
- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'], select the **Constraints** property group and click the **Create** button. In the menu, select a duration, interaction, time, or simple constraint. The constraint [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] is displayed.
- In the diagram palette, under the Common category, expand the Constraint command and select the Duration Constraint, Time Constraint, or Constraint button and create it directly on the action shape.

If a constraint is displayed in the **Constraints** property group of the element [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'], it means this constraint is applied for the element. If it is displayed in the **Inner Elements** list, this constraint is only owned by the element.

##### Editing a duration interval of the constraint

To edit the duration interval of the constraint

1. Right-click the element shape and select Specification.
2. In the Specification window, select the Constraints property group.
3. Edit the duration interval on the left side of the Specification window in the Specification column.

##### Applying an existing constraint

To apply a constraint to an element

1. In the chosen element's [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] , select the Constraints property group and click the Apply button. The Select Constraint dialog opens.
2. Select a constraint or create a new one.
3. Click OK when you are done.

#### PANEL: Related Pages

Related Pages

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Class diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Use Case' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Use Case diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Sequence diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Activity diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with Actions' space='MD2024xR3']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:layout><ac:layout-section ac:type="two_right_sidebar"><ac:layout-cell><p>You can edit constraints in the <strong>Constraints</strong> property group of the containing element Specification window, in the constraint’s Specification window, or double click the selected constraint and edit it on the diagram pane directly.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="5cd4774f-d718-4558-a0be-70f3582fef06"><ac:rich-text-body><p>To see the constraint expression, make sure the <strong>Show Constraint</strong> value is set to true, in the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Symbol Properties dialog" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:link-body><strong>Symbol Properties</strong> dialog</ac:link-body></ac:link>.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p>In this section, see the following procedures:</p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="toc" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="f4b1ab44-7973-4607-ae6a-29a971acd416" /></p><h3>Defining a new constraint</h3><p>To define a new constraint, do one of the following</p><hr /><ul><li>In the Containment Tree, from the element shortcut menu, select <strong>Create Element</strong> &gt; <strong>Constraint</strong>.</li><li>In the <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Specification window" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link>, select the <strong>Inner Elements</strong> property group and click the <strong>Create</strong> button (select Constraint from the list, if needed). If it is displayed in the <strong>Inner Elements</strong> list, this constraint is only owned by the element.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Editing a duration interval of the constraint</h3><p>To edit the duration interval of the constraint</p><hr /><ol><li>Right-click the element shape and select Specification.</li><li>In the Specification window, select the <strong>Constraints</strong> property group.</li><li>Edit the duration interval on the left side of the Specification window in the Specification column.</li></ol><h3>Applying an existing constraint</h3><p>To apply a constraint to an element</p><hr /><ol><li>In the chosen element's <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Specification window" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link>, select the <strong>Constraints</strong> property group and click the <strong>Apply</strong> button. The <strong>Select Constraint</strong> dialog opens. </li><li>Select a constraint or create a new one.</li><li>Click <strong>OK</strong> when you are done.</li></ol></ac:layout-cell><ac:layout-cell><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="panel" ac:schema-version="1" <!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150315 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
````
## PAGE 01254: Working with dependencies

- page_id: `227150315`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150315/Working+with+dependencies
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:33.816+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Dependency
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

###### Element Import

To draw the Element Import dependency

1. Open or create the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package diagram' space='MD2024xR3'] .
2. In the diagram, select or create at least two packages. When using created packages, simply drag and drop the packages onto your diagram pane and name them as you wish.
3. On the Package diagram palette, expand the Package Merge button [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.17.43 PM.png'] and select the Element Import button [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.17.54 PM.png'] . [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.33.08 PM.png']

###### Access

An Access relationship shows that elements can only be accessed from a package, and it cannot be referenced.

To draw the Access dependency

1. Open or create the Package diagram.
2. On the Package diagram palette, expand the Package Merge button [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.17.43 PM.png'] and select the Package Import button [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.28.54 PM.png'] .
3. Draw the dependency on your diagram pane between two packages.
4. Select the Package Import dependency, open its [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] , and set the Visibility property to private . [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.31.03 PM.png']

###### Deployment

To draw a deployment relationship

1. Create a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Deployment diagram' space='MD2024xR3'] .
2. On the Deployment diagram pane, create a [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Node' space='MD2024xR3'] and an [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Artifacts' space='CBMP2024xR3'] by dragging and dropping each one onto the diagram pane.
3. Click the Deployment button [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.42.33 PM.png'] and draw a deployment link from the node to the artifact. [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-13 at 9.43.10 PM.png']

To display the deployed artifacts on the node instance shape

Do one of the following:

- On the diagram pane, select the node instance symbol, then click the Compartments button [ATTACHMENT filename='compartments.png'] (usually it is displayed on the top left corner of the symbol). In the opened menu, select the Deployed Elements .
- On the diagram pane, right-click the node instance and from the shortcut menu, select Symbol Properties . Then in the Symbol Properties dialog, set the Suppress Deployed Elements property value to false .

#### PANEL: On this page

On this page

## PAGE 01255: Working with Enterprise Architect Import

- page_id: `227148607`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148607/Working+with+Enterprise+Architect+Import
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T12:32:57.324+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects > Importing data from other UML tools and formats > Enterprise Architect Import
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Note

479168392

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Note

100.00002%

479168395

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Note

479168394

Enterprise Architect Import (EA) will automatically load when you start a program. You can use it to import UML 2.1 XMI 2.1 to your modeling tool.

To import Enterprise Architect UML XMI file

1. On the main menu of the modeling tool, click File > Import From > Enterprise Architect UML2.1 XMI 2.1 File . The Import Enterprise Architect Files dialog opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='Import Enterprise Architect Files.png']
2. In the dialog, you must specify:
  - The input file - the XMI file exported from Enterprise Architecture NoteEnterprise Architect Import supports the EA XMI files exported with the option specified as: XMI Type = **UML2.1(XMI 2.1).**
  - The output file name
  - A conversion option
3. Click Import to import the file.

The following table describes conversion options:

| Conversion Option | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Switch aggregation side | To configure the aggregation switch-side. This option is recommended for XMI files exported from EA 7.1. |
| Exclude EA specific data | To exclude all EA-specific data from being imported (see Transforming EA Specific Data to see a list of EA specific-data that can be transformed into UML elements with stereotypes). |
| Open project after conversion | To load the output project file once the conversion process has been completed. |
| Generate conversion log | To generate a conversion log and save it in the same folder as the output file. The same conversion information will also be displayed on the Notification Window.NoteYou can open the window by pressing Ctrl + M. |

479168391

**Related pages**
