<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227149098 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01256: Working with Execution Specifications

- page_id: `227149098`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149098/Working+with+Execution+Specifications
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2018-11-12T09:53:54.602+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > UML diagrams > Sequence diagram
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

872285712

872285714

438547513

**On this page**

872285713

The activation bars represent real model elements - Behavior and Action Execution Specifications. This benefits of using UML Execution Specifications are:

- Navigation. By double-clicking the activation bars (Behavior Execution Specifications) you can navigate from a sequence diagram to other behavior diagrams.
- Time and Duration Constraints can be attached to Behavior and Action Execution Specifications.

This method of modeling is optional. By default, the modeling approach where activation bars represent lifelines is used.

To switch to the new mode with activation bars representing UML Execution Specifications

- In the Sequence diagram palette, click the **Enable Execution Specification Modeling** button. This action enables the new modeling mode for each Sequence diagram individually.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

- When you switch to this modeling approach, you will not be able to return to previous modeling method.
- If you open the Sequence Diagram with the activation bars representing UML Execution Specifications with the modeling tool version 19.0, such diagram will be read-only.

After you have enabled the Execution Specification Modeling, the activation bars in Sequence diagram represent:

- Behavior Execution Specification
- Action Execution Specification

You can refactor one Execution Specification to another at any time.

##### Setting behaviors or actions on the Execution Specifications

From the Containment tree, you can drag the Behavior or Action on the Execution Specification.

When you drag the behavior:

- If the activation bar represents Behavior Execution Specification, the dropped behavior is set for the behavior property of the Behavior Execution Specification.
- If the activation bar represents Action Execution Specification, the Action Execution Specification is converted to the Behavior Execution Specification and then the dropped behavior is set for the behavior property of the Behavior Execution Specification.

When you drag the action:

- If the activation bar represents Action Execution Specification, the dropped action is set for the action property of the Action Execution Specification.
- If the activation bar represents Behavior Execution Specification, the Behavior Execution Specification is converted to the Action Execution Specification and then dropped action is set for the action property of the Action Execution Specification.

Once the behavior or action is set for the Execution Specification, you can easily navigate to the diagrams of the set behavior or action.

To navigate to the behavior diagram

- Double-click the Behavior Execution Specification.

To navigate to the activity diagram

- Double-click the Action Execution Specification.

##### Setting the Behavior Execution Specification behavior by adding an operation for the message

When you have an operation with a method, you can add that operation to the message and the method is set as a behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification at the end of the message.

To set an operation with a method

1. In the Sequence diagram, draw a message between Behavior Execution Specifications.
2. In the Containment tree, select an operation with a method and drag it to the message.
3. Open the Specification window of the Behavior Execution Specification which is at the end of the message. In the Behavior property cell, the operation method is set as a behavior.

- If you change the operation to a different one that has a different method, that method will overwrite the behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification.
- If you change the operation to a different one that has no method, the previously set method will remain as a behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification.

##### Drawing the Time and Duration constraints

When you draw new Time constraints in a Sequence diagram (from the diagram palette):

- If you click near the top of the activation bar, the constrainedElement will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and firstEvent=true .
- If you click near the bottom of the activation bar, the constrainedElement will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and firstEvent=false .

When you draw new Duration constraints in a Sequence diagram (from the diagram palette):

- If you click near the top of the activation bar, the constrainedElement [i] will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and firstEvent[i]=true.
- If you click near the bottom of the activation bar, the constrainedElement [i] will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and firstEvent[i]=false .

872285711

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating diagrams' space='MD2024xR3']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-layer" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="d945e577-4ee4-4e31-9e87-d50c7c4aed4f"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">872285712</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-column" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="f1add55b-d7be-4722-91ee-9e13dd4cd030"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">872285714</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="e511b86f-5d6f-4bd3-b0e0-1238a967bb54"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">438547513</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>On this page</strong></p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="toc" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="4811e4f0-bd7a-4116-9919-03a94be4c393" /></p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="012a4e2e-c918-4f90-bd4d-0a2e7fef3aba"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">872285713</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>The activation bars represent real model elements - Behavior and Action Execution Specifications. This benefits of using UML Execution Specifications are:</p><ul><li>Navigation. By double-clicking the activation bars (Behavior Execution Specifications) you can navigate from a sequence diagram to other behavior diagrams.</li><li>Time and Duration Constraints can be attached to Behavior and Action Execution Specifications.</li></ul><p>This method of modeling is optional. By default, the modeling approach where activation bars represent lifelines is used.</p><p><br /></p><p>To switch to the new <ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="d850ac0d-b43f-4460-b161-c38586e80850">mode</ac:inline-comment-marker> with activation bars representing UML Execution Specifications</p><hr /><ul><li><p class="auto-cursor-target">In the Sequence diagram palette, click the <strong>Enable Execution Specification Modeling</strong> button.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="58e47dac-dac6-42fa-92ea-38184a61dc45"><ac:rich-text-body><p>This action enables the new modeling mode for each Sequence diagram individually.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></li></ul><p><ac:image ac:border="true" ac:height="146" ac:width="306"><ri:attachment ri:filename="enable_execution_specification_modeling.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Execution Specifications" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="7b999763-ddc6-4c3f-82c3-01042633be0a"><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li>When you switch to this modeling approach, you <strong>will not be able</strong> to return to previous modeling method.</li><li>If you open the Sequence Diagram with the activation bars representing UML Execution Specifications with the modeling tool version 19.0, such diagram will be read-only.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p>After you have enabled the Execution Specification Modeling, the activation bars in Sequence diagram represent:</p><ul><li>Behavior Execution Specification</li><li>Action Execution Specification</li></ul><p>You can refactor one Execution Specification to another at any time.</p><h3>Setting behaviors or actions on the Execution Specifications</h3><p>From the Containment tree, you can drag the <ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="4c805416-586d-426a-9620-1c245aa60da2">Behavior or Action</ac:inline-comment-marker> on the Execution Specification.</p><p>When you drag the behavior:</p><ul><li>If the activation bar represents Behavior Execution Specification, the dropped behavior is set for the <strong>behavior</strong> property of the Behavior Execution Specification.</li><li>If the activation bar represents Action Execution Specification, the Action Execution Specification is converted to the Behavior Execution Specification and then the dropped behavior is set for the <strong>behavior</strong> property of the Behavior Execution Specification.</li></ul><p>When you drag the action:</p><ul><li>If the activation bar represents Action Execution Specification, the dropped action is set for the <strong>action</strong> property of the Action Execution Specification.</li><li>If the activation bar represents Behavior Execution Specification, the Behavior Execution Specification is converted to the Action Execution Specification and then dropped action is set for the <strong>action</strong> property of the Action Execution Specification.</li></ul><p>Once the behavior or action is set for the Execution Specification, you can easily navigate to the diagrams of the set behavior or action.</p><p><br /></p><p>To navigate to the behavior diagram</p><hr /><ul><li>Double-click the Behavior Execution Specification. </li></ul><p><br /></p><p>To navigate to the activity diagram</p><hr /><ul><li>Double-click the Action Execution Specification.</li></ul><h3><br />Setting the Behavior Execution Specification behavior by adding an operation for the message</h3><p>When you have an operation with a method, you can add that operation to the message and the method is set as a behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification at the end of the message.</p><p><br /></p><p>To set an operation with a method</p><hr /><ol><li>In the Sequence diagram, draw a message between Behavior Execution Specifications.</li><li>In the Containment tree, select an operation with a method and drag it to the message.</li><li>Open the Specification window of the Behavior Execution Specification which is at the end of the message. In the Behavior property cell, the operation method is set as a behavior.</li></ol><p><br /></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="note" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="b3de7296-d1a8-417f-93a7-2047d6f3350b"><ac:rich-text-body><ul><li><ac:inline-comment-marker ac:ref="bd57754a-d664-4f35-8d33-c5828623a335">If you change the operation to a different one that has a different method, that method will overwrite the behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification.</ac:inline-comment-marker></li><li>If you change the operation to a different one that has no method, the previously set method will remain as a behavior of the Behavior Execution Specification.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><h3>Drawing the Time and Duration constraints</h3><p>When you draw new Time constraints in a Sequence diagram (from the diagram palette):</p><ul><li>If you click near the top of the activation bar, the constrainedElement will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and <em>firstEvent=true</em>.</li><li>If you click near the bottom of the activation bar, the constrainedElement will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and <em>firstEvent=false</em>.</li></ul><p>When you draw new Duration constraints in a Sequence diagram (from the diagram palette):</p><ul><li>If you click near the top of the activation bar, the constrainedElement<span class="error">[i]</span> will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and <em>firstEvent<span class="error">[i]</span>=true.</em></li><li>If you click near the bottom of the activation bar, the constrainedElement<span class="error">[i]</span> will be set to the Execution Specification of that bar, and <em>firstEvent<span class="error">[i]</span>=false</em>.</li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="7600f0d1-e9f6-4575-9e35-8ddb6b2dba9a"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">872285711</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><ul><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Creating diagrams" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link></li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227151116 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01257: Working with generic numbering mechanism

- page_id: `227151116`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227151116/Working+with+generic+numbering+mechanism
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2025-02-20T14:07:06.391+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with model elements > Generic numbering mechanism
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

With the generic numbering mechanism you can number the elements by setting their IDs. There are two element numbering modes: [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Automatic numbering' space='MD2024xR3']and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Manual numbering' space='MD2024xR3']. If you choose the automatic numbering mode, a number for an element will be created automatically according to a predefined numbering format. Using the manual numbering mode you can create a custom number format for the element.

Make sure that [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating Numbering Customizations' space='MD2024xR3'] are already created.

**Related pages**

true

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html

There are two element numbering modes: <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Automatic numbering" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[automatic ]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>and <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Manual numbering" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[manual]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link>. If you choose the automatic numbering mode, a number for an element will be created automatically according to a predefined numbering format. Using the manual numbering mode you can create a custom number format for the element.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="54153b7d-f645-4ace-9167-986af3ed7caf"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Make sure that <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Creating Numbering Customizations" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /><ac:plain-text-link-body><![CDATA[numbering customizations]]></ac:plain-text-link-body></ac:link> are already created.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><p><br /></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section><ac:layout-section ac:type="single"><ac:layout-cell><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="children" ac:schema-version="2" ac:macro-id="6815dda7-87ef-435b-bb99-610871778df6"><ac:parameter ac:name="all">true</ac:parameter></ac:structured-macro></p></ac:layout-cell></ac:layout-section></ac:layout>

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150440 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01258: Working with Links

- page_id: `227150440`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150440/Working+with+Links
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2017-07-09T21:27:52.930+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Link
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

To create a link

1. Create an [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Object diagram' space='MD2024xR3'] .
2. In the diagram pane, create two Instance shapes by dragging and dropping the element onto the diagram pane. Select any Classifier you would like.
3. Draw a Link between the two Instance shapes.
4. The Select Association dialog opens. Select Association dialogThe Select Association dialog displays associations that are created between the classifiers of the Link.
5. Select the appropriate association and click OK .
6. The Create Slots dialog opens. Select the appropriate slots and click OK .

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Example of a link between two Instance shapes.

To create slots on a link

1. In the Object diagram's diagram pane, create two Instance shapes by dragging and dropping the element onto the diagram pane. Select any Classifier you would like.
2. Draw a Link between the two Instance shapes. The Select Associations dialog opens.
3. In the Select Association dialog, select the appropriate associations then click OK .
4. The Create Slots dialog opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-20 at 12.43.56 PM.png']
5. Select the slots. Create Slots dialogThe Create Slots dialog displays the roles of the association that is created between the classifiers of the Link.[IMAGE alt='' src='']
6. Click OK. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

#### NOTE: Automatic Creation of Slots on Links

Automatic Creation of Slots on Links

- The slots on the Link are created automatically only if the Automatically Create Slots of Link option is set to true . For more information, read the instructions on how to turn on automatic creation of slots in Links further on in this page.
- The slots on a Link are created automatically only when the Link references the association. For more information read on how to create a Link at the top of this page.

To turn on automatic creation of slots in links

1. In the window, click Options > Environment . The Environment Options dialog opens.
2. In the General options group, under the Editing subgroup, set the Automatically Create Slots in Link option value to true .

To display slot values on a link

1. Right-click on a Link. Select Symbol Properties . The Symbol Properties dialog opens.
2. Deselect the Suppress Slots check box, so it says false .
3. The result should look something like the figure below. [ATTACHMENT filename='Screen Shot 2017-06-20 at 1.21.41 PM.png']

#### NOTE: Suppress Slots Default Value

Suppress Slots Default Value

- The default value of the Suppress Slots option is true , that is, slots are not displayed on a Link.
- Slots on a Link are displayed in the following form: {< slot1 name > = < slot values >, < slot2 name > = <slot values> , ... }

#### TIP: Edit Compartment

Edit Compartment

You can select to display or hide an individual slot in the Compartment Edit dialog.

To open the Compartment Edit dialog

- Select the link on a diagram pane and on its [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Shortcut menu' space='CDH185'] , click Edit Compartment > Slots.

To change a link end

1. On a diagram pane, select an end of a Link and move it to the other target.
2. The Link is connected to the other target.

#### PANEL: Related Pages

Related Pages

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Displaying internal structure on structured classifiers' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Link' space='MD2024xR3']

#### PANEL: Related References

Related References

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Object diagram' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Active Validation Rules for Links' space='MD2024xR3']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150800 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01259: Working with model elements

- page_id: `227150800`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150800/Working+with+model+elements
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-01-30T10:29:36.614+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Containment Tree

29726528

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Containment Tree

29726530

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Containment Tree

29726529

#### EXCERPT: Containment Tree

INLINE

The chapter outlines various methods of working with your model's elements. You will find detailed instructions on creating and defining model elements, default property values, extracting, defining hyperlinks, etc. You will also learn how the modeling tool shortcut menus, toolbar, and browser enable you to easily edit model elements.

[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']true

To create elements in the Containment tree

1. In the Containment Tree, right-click the element owner where you want to create a new model element.
2. From the shortcut menu, select Create Element .
3. A list with available elements appears. Select the element you need or start typing an element name in the Search box to find it faster.
4. Type the name of the element.

You can also create an element directly on the diagram pane. In this case, a symbol of the element and the element in the diagram owner is created.

To create elements on the diagram pane

1. Open the diagram or create a new diagram where you want to create a new model element.
2. From the diagram palette, select an element and drag it on the diagram pane. The element symbol is created.
3. Click the symbol and type the element name.

#### TIP: Containment Tree

Containment Tree

Please note, the new element is created in the Model Browser as well.

29726527

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating diagrams' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Understanding the user interface' space='MD2024xR3']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-layer" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c5e75bf4-6296-4493-a3fb-c07f5c1c2fb8"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">29726528</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-column" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="fc0b4119-894a-4efa-97ed-3cfb093cd1b1"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">29726530</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="de1a54d5-0cc8-405c-996f-ea0bdd8a8a4c"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">29726529</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><ac:structured-macro ac:name="excerpt" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="93905398-59f1-4de1-913f-cf189cd6f7ca"><ac:parameter ac:name="atlassian-macro-output-type">INLINE</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>The chapter outlines various methods of working with your model's elements. Select the element you need or start typing an element name in the <strong>Search</strong> box to find it faster.</li><li>Type the name of the element.</li></ol><p><br /></p><p>You can also create an element directly on the diagram pane. In this case, a symbol of the element and the element in the diagram owner is created.</p><p><br /></p><p>To create elements on the diagram pane</p><hr /><ol><li>Open the diagram or create a new diagram where you want to create a new model element.</li><li>From the diagram palette, select an element and drag it on the diagram pane. The element symbol is created. </li><li>Click the symbol and type the element name.</li></ol><ac:structured-macro ac:name="tip" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="7662a924-8310-40e7-bcbd-940efe612c63"><ac:parameter ac:name="title">Containment Tree</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p>Please note, the new element is created in the Model Browser as well.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><ac:structured-macro ac:name="content-block" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="6ae807fa-ccde-47d1-bb2a-7e8333539c73"><ac:parameter ac:name="id">29726527</ac:parameter><ac:rich-text-body><p><strong>Related pages</strong></p><ul><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="UML elements" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link></li><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Creating diagrams" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link></li><li><ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="Understanding the user interface" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ac:link></li></ul></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227148489 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01260: Working with model elements in the Model Browser

- page_id: `227148489`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148489/Working+with+model+elements+in+the+Model+Browser
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:23.340+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Getting started > Understanding the user interface > Model Browser
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1426024704

1426024708

1426024707

INLINE

In the Model Browser, you can do the various actions with model elements, such as rename, cut, copy, delete, and others. These actions are available from the particular model element shortcut menu. See the list of concrete actions in the following table.

| Command | Function |
| --- | --- |
| Rename | Switches the element name into the edit mode. You can also press F2 for this. |
| Copy | Copies the selected element. |
| Copy URL | Copies a model element URL to a clipboard. |
| Copy Element Hyperlink | Copies the hyperlink of the selected element. |
| Cut | Cuts the selected element. |
| Paste | Pastes the copied element. |
| Delete | Deletes the selected element. |

To copy/cut and paste the selected model element between different projects

1. Select the model element in the Model Browser. 
 2. From the model element shortcut menu, select **Copy** or **Cut**. 
 3. Open the project to which you want to paste the selected element(s). 
 4. Select the container, where you wish to paste the element(s). 
 5. From the container's shortcut menu, select **Paste**.

To change the location of an element in the Model Browser

1. Select the element in the Model Browser. 
 2. Drag it to the new location (possible owner).

1426024703

**Related pages**

- Model Browser

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227148596 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01262: Working with multiple projects

- page_id: `227148596`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148596/Working+with+multiple+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-02-01T16:15:19.836+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects > Creating projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1428492948

1428492951

1428492950

INLINE

You may need to manage several projects at the same time, and the modeling tool allows you to do that easily. All open projects are held in separate workspaces. Different active projects may exchange data. Entities from one project can be copied or moved to another.

To switch between open projects, do one of the following

- From File menu, select Switch Projects and then click the name of the project you want to switch to.
- On the main toolbar, click [ATTACHMENT filename='switch_projects_button.png'] and then select the name of the project you want to switch to. [ATTACHMENT filename='switching_between_projects.png']

To close all open projects

- Select Close All Projects from the File menu. The Question message appears.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Choose the way your projects will be closed:

| Yes | The project you are currently closing will be saved (its name appears in the question). The dialog is displayed again when the next project closes. |
| --- | --- |
| Yes To All | Save all projects without prompting. The Save dialog will not appear for each open project. |
| No | Project you are currently closing will not be saved. The dialog is displayed again when the next project closes. |
| No To All | All the projects will be closed without saving or further prompting. |
| Cancel | Cancel saving projects. |

To exchange model elements between open projects

- Use the Cut , Copy , and Paste commands from the Edit menu or the selected element's shortcut menu, or the appropriate shortcut keys: Ctrl + X, Ctrl + C, Ctrl + V.

1428492947

**Rrelated pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Creating projects' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Project Properties dialog' space='MD2024xR3']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150568 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01263: Working with packages

- page_id: `227150568`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150568/Working+with+packages
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2017-07-09T21:49:46.131+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Package
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

You can [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3'] in the package [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3']. In the same window, you can find the description of each property. Descriptions are displayed in the description area of the Specification window.

You can conveniently [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Package import' space='MD2024xR3'] to find the elements you're looking for in the type selection list.

The procedures below illustrate how to work with packages:

##### Adding inner elements

To add inner elements to the selected package

1. In the Package Specification window, select the Inner Elements property group.
2. Click the Create button, and select an element you wish to add. The selected element Specification window will open.
3. Define the properties you need.
4. Click Back to return to Package Specification window.

##### Changing the package header position

To change the package header position

- In the Symbol Properties dialog, set the Header Position property to:
  - Top to place a package header at the top of a package shape.
  - In Tab to place a package header in a package tab.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Showing the list of elements assigned to a package on its shape

To show the list of elements assigned to a package on the package shape

- From the selected package shortcut menu, choose Show Inner Elements List .

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

##### Displaying inner elements inside package shape

To display the inner elements of a package in a diagram

1. Select a single package shape on the diagram pane.
2. Open the Select Inner Elements dialog by doing one of the following: - From its shortcut menu, select Display > Display Inner Elements . - On the diagram toolbar, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] and select Display Inner Elements.
3. In the dialog, select the elements that you want to display inside the package shape. [ATTACHMENT filename='select_inner_elements.png']
4. Click **OK**. 
The selected elements are displayed on the shape of the selected package. 
[IMAGE alt='' src='']

The rake icon [IMAGE alt='' src=''] is displayed on the shape if the package refers to another package diagrams. The rake icon isn’t shown by default, therefore, you need to set the **[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Displaying rake icon' space='MD2024xR3']** property value to *true* in the **[CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Symbol Properties dialog' space='MD2024xR3']** dialog.

#### PANEL: Related Pages

Related Pages

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='UML elements' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227148862 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01264: Working with partially loaded projects

- page_id: `227148862`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148862/Working+with+partially+loaded+projects
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2018-03-20T14:30:37.970+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects > Project partitioning > Managing used projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

418017743

418017745

418017744

To increase modeling efficiency when working with very large projects, you can work with partially loaded used projects. This may help decrease memory consumption.

Here, “large” is tens of thousands of classes and other complex elements. If counting all small elements, such as properties, methods, method parameters, several hundreds of thousands of elements is considered a large project. Note that diagrams are large elements. A project consisting of 1000 or more complex diagrams should be considered large.

You can unload a particular used project at any time when working with a large partitioned project.

To unload a used project from a project

- Right-click the selected used project, and select Project Usages > Unload .

Not loaded (or unloaded) used projects can be loaded in a project anytime. For more information about managing used projects, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Managing used projects' space='MD2024xR3'].

To load a used project in a project

- From the unloaded used project's shortcut menu, select Used Projects and then Load Used Project.

When the used project is neither loaded nor unloaded, there can be some model elements left from the used project. These elements are not editable and are characterized by a small M letter in the upper left corner of their icon (see the following figure).

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Notation of unloaded used project elements (fragment of Containment tree)

These are the so-called “proxy” elements of the original elements from the used project. Instead of the original model elements, the proxy is a lightweight surrogate that carries only the name and kind of the model element information. These proxies are left in place of the original used project elements and are dedicated to maintaining model integrity (ensuring that there are no dangling ends of relationships, types of properties do not disappear, etc.) while the used project is not accessible or not loaded.

There are 4 used project loading modes:

- Always load (default). In this mode, used projects are always loaded when you open the project. They can be unloaded if necessary.
- Autoload . A used project is not loaded while the project using it is loaded. However, our modeling tool monitors user activities in the project and tries to guess when you might want to use the model piece from the unloaded used project. For example, if you search and find usages/dependencies, reports, metrics, transformations, or code engineering actions with a scope that touches the unloaded used project, our modeling tool will load that used project.
- Autoload with prompt . This mode differs from the **Autoload** mode in that our modeling tool asks you before loading the used project.
- Manual load . A used project is not loaded while the project using it is loaded. It can be loaded using the **Load** used project command (described above).

To change the used project loading mode

1. From the Options menu, select Used Projects. The Used Projects dialog opens.
2. In the used project's tree, select a used project.
3. In the Used Project Load Mode area, select the appropriate loading mode.

Always load

Occasionally used projects should be set in **Autoload** mode (or **Autoload with prompt** to have more control on loading behavior). Very rarely used projects can be set in the **Manual load** mode. Another frequent case where used projects can be set to **Manual load** mode occurs when the used projects represent a software library that is not expected to change.

418017742

**Related pages**

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Maintaining decomposed model integrity' space='MD2024xR3']

## PAGE 01265: Working with paths and relationships

- page_id: `227149960`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`

569613428

569613430

569613429

The difference between relationships and [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Paths' space='MD2024xR3'] is that a relationship is a link between model elements, while the path is a representation of the relationship on a diagram.

You can learn how to work with paths and relationships on the following pages:

## PAGE 01267: Working with projects

- page_id: `227148585`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148585/Working+with+projects

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

1428208479

1428208482

1428208480

INLINE

##### Basic concepts

The following table presents more in-depth descriptions of further material.

| Concept | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Project | A physical working unit that consists of a model, model visualizations (diagrams, tables, matrices, etc.), configuration data and references to other elements residing in used projects. |
| Used project(up to 18.0 – Module) | A project that has one or more shared packages. Used projects are created for the purpose of decomposing projects into parts in order to manage each part separately and/or reuse those parts in other projects.A used project is a role that one project plays in the composition of another project. It is not a type of project. Each used project can be opened and modified separately. |

1428208478

**Related pages**

## PAGE 01268: Working with QT

- page_id: `227154784`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227154784/Working+with+QT
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2024-02-01T16:48:36.065+01:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > Code Engineering > C++ Code Engineering > Project Constraints
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

To reverse engineer QT code, we recommend you set the**Parse Includes**option to "false". You must also set the modeling tool's preprocessor to skip some QT macros ("**Options**"-> "**Project**"-> "**C++ Language Options**"-> "**Use explicit macros**").

**[IMAGE alt='' src='']**

The modeling tool has already defined some default skipped macros for QT.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227148936 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01270: Working with standard profiles

- page_id: `227148936`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227148936/Working+with+standard+profiles
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2026-06-18T10:17:02.652+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with projects
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

All profiles and libraries that are bundled with the modeling tool are considered as standard/system resources, non-modifiable and essential for the proper performance of the tool. 
 
We highly recommend not to modify our provided standard profiles and libraries as it could cause problems on version updates, plugins, core malfunctions, and model corruptions.

Users will be warned on any intentional or unintentional attempt to modify profiles when:

- Opening profiles as projects.
- Using profiles in the read-write mode.
- Importing profiles into a project.
- Merging projects, and several other occasions.

##### Plugin and Profile Versions

Standard profiles are usually upgraded to support the latest versions of the specification of standards they represent (for example, SysML 1.2 or UML 2.4) in every modeling tool release cycle. The modeling tool application, plugins code and behavior are modified accordingly to reflect these changes.

There is a high probability that the latest version of a modeling tool or plugin won't work with earlier or later profile versions and may cause unpredictable behavior or even model distortions. For example, SysML plugin 16.5 requires SysML Profile 16.5, as it could malfunction when using SysML Profile 16.0 or 16.6.

To protect users from such inconveniences, every project stores information about profiles or plugins versions that were used to create it and are required to load data correctly. Every standard profile has a version number. Normally, it's the same as modeling tool (or plugin) version number.

The modeling tool requires using corresponding profile and software versions. If you use plugins or profiles that are obsolete, you will see a warning message. If you are missing certain plugins or profiles, Resource Manager with selected resources to install is launched automatically, so you can install missing resources in just few clicks.

If new versions of plugins are not purchased or you simply don't want to install it, but need to take a look at the project content, warnings may be ignored and such project may be loaded. In this case, proxy elements for missing profile elements will be created to retain missing references. Missing custom diagrams will be loaded as regular UML diagrams or will be restricted for review.

Do not save such projects! Use them for preview only.

The modeling tool is forward-compatible; old projects will be loaded/converted without any warnings if you have the latest versions of the corresponding plugins and profiles.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

````html
<p>All profiles and libraries that are bundled with the modeling tool are considered as standard/system resources, non-modifiable and essential for the proper performance of the tool. <br class="atl-forced-newline" /><br class="atl-forced-newline" />We highly recommend not to modify our provided standard profiles and libraries as it could cause problems on version updates, plugins, core malfunctions, and model corruptions.</p><p>Users will be warned on any intentional or unintentional attempt to modify profiles when:</p><ul><li>Opening profiles as projects.</li><li>Using profiles in the read-write mode.</li><li>Importing profiles into a project.</li><li>Merging projects, and several other occasions.</li></ul><h3>Plugin and Profile Versions</h3><p>Standard profiles are usually upgraded to support the latest versions of the specification of standards they represent (for example, SysML 1.2 or UML 2.4) in every modeling tool release cycle. For example, SysML plugin 16.5 requires SysML Profile 16.5, as it could malfunction when using SysML Profile 16.0 or 16.6.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" />To protect users from such inconveniences, every project stores information about profiles or plugins versions that were used to create it and are required to load data correctly. Every standard profile has a version number. Normally, it's the same as modeling tool (or plugin) version number.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" />The modeling tool requires using corresponding profile and software versions. If you use plugins or profiles that are obsolete, you will see a warning message. If you are missing certain plugins or profiles, Resource Manager with selected resources to install is launched automatically, so you can install missing resources in just few clicks.</p><p><br class="atl-forced-newline" />If new versions of plugins are not purchased or you simply don't want to install it, but need to take a look at the project content, warnings may be ignored and such project may be loaded. In this case, proxy elements for missing profile elements will be created to retain missing references. Missing custom diagrams will be loaded as regular UML diagrams or will be restricted for review.</p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="warning" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="6f8f0208-aa39-442c-aefd-eb8701f3b275"><ac:rich-text-body><p>Do not save such projects! Use them for preview only.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro><p style="text-align: left;">The modeling tool is forward-compatible; old projects will be loaded/converted without any warnings if you have the latest versions of the corresponding plugins and profiles.</p><p style="text-align: left;"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Auto updated profiles.png" /></ac:image></p>
````

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227149104 space=MD2024xR3 version=1 -->
## PAGE 01271: Working with State Machine diagram

- page_id: `227149104`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149104/Working+with+State+Machine+diagram
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-05-16T13:38:32.550+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > UML diagrams > State Machine diagram
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

##### Displaying inner elements

To display inner elements

- When creating a new State Machine diagram, right-click a State Machine element in the Containment tree, select **Create Diagram**, and then click **State****Machine****Diagram**. Inner elements are displayed on the State Machine diagram pane automatically upon creating the first diagram under the State Machine element.
- When modifying a preexisting State Machine diagram, select the diagram pane or the State shape and perform one of the following steps: - From the shortcut menu, click Display > Display Inner Elements . - On the diagram toolbar, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] and select Display Inner Elements .

##### Working with behaviors

You can select Entry, Do Activity, Exit, deferrable triggers, and internal transitions directly in the compartment of the State shape. Thus, you can:

- Draw dependencies among particular behaviors on a state shape.
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Dragging objects' space='MD2024xR3'] from one state shape to another.
- Convert the selected behavior to another.

To convert a behavior to another behavior

1. On a State shape, select a behavior.
2. From the behavior's shortcut menu, select Refactor > Convert To > < behavior >.

### EXACT CONFLUENCE STORAGE SOURCE

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227151004 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01272: Working with Symbol styles

- page_id: `227151004`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227151004/Working+with+Symbol+styles
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:45.185+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Working with model elements > Formatting symbols
- labels: ['style-engine']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Warning

601916684

INLINE

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Warning

601916688

INLINE

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Warning

601916687

INLINE

#### WARNING: Warning

Warning

Before you begin working on symbol styles in a Teamwork Cloud project, you need to lock the symbols styles for edit first.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

In the**Project Options** dialog, click the **Symbol Styles** option group, to expand the tree hierarchy of all the styles defined within the project. You may use as many of these styles as you wish.

**Shape** and **Path** trees have the inner structure to help you find the model element for which you want to change the symbol style. The right side of the dialog contains possible choices and the instruments to manage them.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

Before changing symbol styles, we advise you to make a copy of the default style so you can come back to it if needed. You can make a copy by cloning the default style, which will create a new style. You can make changes in any selected style.

To create a new style by cloning the existing one

1. In the Symbol styles group, select Default style and click the Clone button.
2. Enter a name for the new style.
3. Change options of the new style.

As stated previously, you can create several symbol styles. You can set the desired style to be your default at any time.

To make a selected style your default style

- In the Symbol styles options group, select the style to make the default and click the Make Default button.

You can change Default symbol styles using the **Set Select Symbol Style as Default** button in the diagram toolbar. If you do not see this button, you need to change **Perspective** to the **Full feature** or [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Customizing Perspectives' space='MD2024xR3'].

You can select to apply one of the predefined styles for the existing diagrams.

To apply the selected style

- In the Symbol styles group, select the style you want to apply and click the Apply button.

You can also apply the desired options to selected diagram model elements. Click the **Apply** button in the specific element's pane.

You can move your earlier defined symbol styles between other projects or users. Simply export the defined style and pass it on for other projects or users to import.

To save the created style (export)

1. In the Symbol styles group, click the Export button. The Save dialog opens.
2. Select the location where you wish to export a style.

To import a project style

1. In the Symbol styles group, click the Import button. The Open dialog opens.
2. Select the style you wish to import (*.stl).

601916682

INLINE

**Related pages**

- Symbol Properties dialog
- Symbol styles option group
- Copy and paste symbol style
- Making your own default style for new projects

## PAGE 01273: Working with symbols of model elements

- page_id: `227149954`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149954/Working+with+symbols+of+model+elements
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-09-22T13:25:55.148+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagramming
- labels: ['resize', 'resize-shape']

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Use the Sticky button

569530408

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Use the Sticky button

569530410

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Use the Sticky button

569530409

700349

To draw an element on the diagram pane

1. Select an element button on the diagram palette.
2. Click anywhere on the diagram pane.

To draw several elements of the same type on the diagram pane, do one of the following

#### EXPAND: Use the Shift key

Use the Shift key

1. Press and hold Shift.
2. Click an element button on the diagram palette.
3. Click the diagram pane. With each click, the new element of the same type is drawn.

#### EXPAND: Use the Sticky button

Use the Sticky button

1. On the diagram palette, under the Tools category, click the [ATTACHMENT filename='sticky_button.png'] Sticky button or press Z.
2. From the diagram palette, select an element button.
3. Click the diagram pane. With each click, the new element of the same type is drawn.

To draw a symbol of the existing element

1. Activate a diagram on which you wish to draw a symbol.
2. From the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Model Browser' space='MD2024xR3'] , select an item you wish to draw.
3. Drag the selected model element onto the diagram pane.

To specify a name of the element, do one of the following

- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'] , Name property specification cell, type the element name.
- Type the symbol name directly on the selected symbol on the diagram pane.
- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Model Browser' space='MD2024xR3'] , select an element and name it.

To draw several symbols for one element, do one of the following

- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Model Browser' space='MD2024xR3'] , select an element and drag it to the diagram pane. Repeat it if needed.
- On the diagram pane, select a symbol, copy and then paste by pressing Ctrl+C and Ctrl+V.

To resize selected shapes to a preferred size

• Click the shape and then click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] at the corners of the symbol and drag to the preferred size.

To change text and compartments vertical position on shapes

- In the Symbol Properties dialog > Text Vertical Position , select one of the following:
  - Top
  - Center
  - Bottom

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

To delete selected model elements, do one of the following

- From the Edit menu, select Delete .
- On the diagram toolbar, click the [ATTACHMENT filename='delete.png'] Delete button.
- Press Ctrl+D.
- In the Activity and Sequence diagrams, press Delete.

The model elements will be removed from the model with all their data.

To delete selected symbols, do one of the following

- From the Edit menu, select Remove from Diagram .
- On the diagram toolbar, click the [ATTACHMENT filename='remove_from_diagram.png'] Remove from Diagram button.
- Press Delete.

569530407

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Diagramming' space='MD2024xR3']

<!--NOMAGIC_PAGE id=227150703 space=MD2024xR3 version=2 -->
## PAGE 01274: Working with Template

- page_id: `227150703`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227150703/Working+with+Template
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:54:39.221+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > UML elements > Template
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Value Specification

502685492

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Value Specification

502685495

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Value Specification

502685494

This section demonstrates how to create a template and how to use it.

Follow these instructions from the first step consistently. If you do not, and if you do not define the template parameter, you will not be able to draw a template binding relationship. You can omit optional procedures only.

#### INFO: Precondition

Precondition

Let’s assume you already have an element to which you want to apply a template. This element is an actual element. The actual element can be a classifier, package, or operation.

To create and apply a template to an actual element, see the following procedures:

- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with Template' space='MD2024xR3']
- [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Working with Template' space='MD2024xR3']

In the following procedures, we will show you how to create a template with parameters and how to define these parameters.

TemplateTo create a template

1. Create or select a template element for which you will create template parameters.
2. Open the element's [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Specification window' space='MD2024xR3'].
3. Change the property display mode to**All**,if it is not changed already. The**Template Parameters** property group appears in the property group list.
4. Click the Template Parameters property group.
5. To add a new template parameter, click the Create button. The Select Template Parameter Type dialog opens. [ATTACHMENT filename='template_select_element.png']
6. In the Model tree, select an existing or create a new type of the template parameter. Template ParameterIf you do not want to specify the concrete template parameter type, you can select the*Class*type (the*Class*from the UML metamodel). When the*Class*type is specified, type is not displayed on the diagram pane. Only the name of the template parameter is represented.If you need to select one of the UML metamodel elements, such as *Class*, be sure to clear the **Hide Uncommon Elements** and **Exclude Used Projects** commands (as in the preceding figure). For more information, read [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Selecting elements' space='MD2024xR3'].
7. Click OK . The template parameter is created. The name of the template parameter is defined automatically by compounding the T letter and the name of the template parameter type - T<type name> . For example, TInteger . You can change the name of the template parameter if you need to. [ATTACHMENT filename='template_parameter.png']
8. (Optional) Assign the default value to the created template parameter. More InformationFor more information about symbol representation properties, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Formatting symbols' space='MD2024xR3']. Value SpecificationTo assign a particular value of the value specification, you must specify a Value Specification first and then type its particular value in the Actual value cell. For more information about Value Specification, read [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Value Specification' space='MD2024xR3'].

After the template is created, you can apply it to the actual element. The following procedures describe how to apply the template to the actual element.

ApplyTo apply a template to an actual element

1. Bind the actual element to the template element. In the diagram palette, click the **Template Binding** button in the Class diagram group or click the **B** shortcut key and draw a template binding relationship from the actual element to the template element. If the **Template Binding** button is not visible, change the the modeling tool's perspective to Full Featured or Software Architect. See the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Customizing and Selecting Perspective' space='MD2024xR3'] page on how to change the perspective.
2. Define a template parameter substitution. Open the Template Binding Specification window and click the Template Parameter Substitutions property group.
3. To add a new template parameter substitution, click the Create button. The Select Template Parameter dialog opens, listing the template parameters of the element to which the template binding relationship is connected. [ATTACHMENT filename='select_template_parameter.png']
4. Select one or more template parameters to add as template parameter substitutions. Click OK to return to the Template Binding Specification window. [ATTACHMENT filename='template_binding_specification_window.png']
5. (Optional) Assign the actual value for each template parameter substitution. More InformationFor more information about specifying property values, see [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Editing property values' space='MD2024xR3']. Value SpecificationTo assign a particular value of the value specification, you must specify a Value Specification first and then type its particular value in the Actual value cell. For more information about Value Specification, read [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Value Specification' space='MD2024xR3'].

502685491

**Related pages**

- Model elements
- Auxiliary Diagram Symbols
- Diagramming

## PAGE 01275: Working with User Interface Modeling diagrams

- page_id: `227149325`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227149325/Working+with+User+Interface+Modeling+diagrams
- version_number: 1
- version_date: `2022-06-08T06:32:32.438+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Diagrams > Extension diagrams > User Interface Modeling diagram
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

86435654565

2142654765

INLINE

1232455425

INLINE

To work with a User Interface Modeling diagram

Do one of the following:

- On the main toolbar, click the Create Diagram button and select User Interface Modeling Diagram . Press Enter.
- In the [CONFLUENCE_PAGE title='Model Browser' space='MD2024xR3'] , click either the Package or the Model. From their shortcut menu select Create Diagram > Other Diagrams > User Interface Modeling Diagram .

After loading a project and creating a diagram, you can add UI modeling elements to the diagram pane.

To add new elements to the User Interface Modeling diagram pane

- Simply drag and drop the elements from the Text, Containers, Button, or Other toolbar.

To load a sample with an already created User Interface model

1. Open either the UI Modeling Samples.mdzip or UI Modeling in System Development.mdzip projects, found in <modeling tool installation directory>\samples\diagrams\User Interface Modeling .
2. After loading the sample, select the diagrams from the Index or Overview d iagrams by clicking the hyperlinks.

## PAGE 01276: Working with Web Publisher 2.0

- page_id: `227153688`
- space_key: `MD2024xR3`
- source_url: https://docs.nomagic.com/spaces/MD2024xR3/pages/227153688/Working+with+Web+Publisher+2.0
- version_number: 2
- version_date: `2025-05-02T11:55:17.937+02:00`
- ancestors: MagicDraw Documentation > User Guide > Report Wizard > Generating Reports from Report Wizard > Web Publisher 2.0 report
- labels: []

### NORMALIZED CONTENT

#### CONTENT-LAYER: Note

1336380615

#### CONTENT-COLUMN: Note

1336380618

#### CONTENT-BLOCK: Note

1336380618

The Web Publisher 2.0 report template comes with predefined variables and their values. Before generating a report based on the Web Publisher 2.0 template, you can add more variables to it, edit the existing ones, or delete those you do not want to include in your report.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Report variables of Web Publisher 2.0.

The following table shows the variable names and values of the Web Publisher 2.0 template.

| Variable | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Author | The report's creator. |
| Title | The report's title. |
| HomeImage | Possible values:Leave it empty or unspecified to use the MagicDraw icon as the homepage image.Enter a diagram name (plain text) to display the selected diagram as the homepage image, for example, Software Development Process.Enter “mdel://” followed by a model element ID to display the element as the homepage image, for example, “mdel://_10_0EAPbeta2_8740266_1126593738250_35764_172”.Enter the absolute path of an image file on your computer to display the image as the homepage image, for example, file://d://picture//image.jpg.Enter the relative path of an image file on your computer to display the image as the homepage image. The relative path starts at the location of the Web Publisher 2.0 template: %APPDATA%\Local\.magicdraw\2021x\data\reports\Web Publisher 2.0\web (%APPDATA% is the location where the user's data are stored, for example, /images/homeimage.jpg).Enter the location of an image on the Web to display the image as the homepage image, for example, http://www.photobucket.com/image.jpg. |
| Diagram as the homepage image. |  |
| UseContextMenu | True: Shows a context menu when right-clicking a diagram element.False: Shows an element specification or opens an element, a diagram, or a page specified in any existing active hyperlink when right-clicking a diagram element. |
| SelectHistoryNode | True: Selects a node when you move backwards or forwards.False: Types "false" if you want it another way. |
| ExportLinkedFile | True: Copies a linked file from a model hyperlink into an output report folder.False: Keeps the link to an absolute path only. |
| ShowAppearsInPage | True: Shows data in a report, and opens the Appears in tab when clicking an element in the Containment tree or a diagram pane. False: Hides the Appears in tab in a generated report. |
| ShowAppliedStereotypes | True: Shows applied stereotypes of elements in the Containment tree.False: Does not show applied stereotypes of elements in the Containment tree. |
| AutoNavigateHyperlink | True: Automatically navigates the active hyperlink of each element. For example, if A has an active hyperlink to B and B has an active hyperlink to C, then C will be shown when you click A.False: The behavior of navigation to active hyperlink is the same as that of MagicDraw. For example, if A has an active hyperlink to B and B has an active hyperlink to C, then B will be shown when you click A. |
| DisplayTreeElementId | True: Shows the property ID of an element in the Containment tree.False: Types "false" if you want it another way. |
| SVGDiagramResizable | True: Resizes SVG images when the browser is minimized.False: Enables SVG image linkable capability, but the resizable capability would be disabled.If the "SVGDiagramResizable" is set to True, the SVG image would be resizable on web browser, but it would not be linkable. |
| SkipElementContext | True: Skips the iteration of all elements to create velocity context classified by customized stereotypes, e.g., $CustomizedStereotypeName.False: Does not skip the iteration of all elements to create velocity context classified by customized stereotypes. |
| GotoLinkByIcon | True: Both the icon and the label of the element in the Containment tree navigate to an active hyperlink.False: The icon element navigates to the element's Specification tab even if there is an active hyperlink. |
| ExportedImageSize | The percentage (from 10 to 1000) of an exported image size. |

WorkingwithWP

The following section contains the instructions on how to work with your Web Publisher report.

To generate a Web Publisher report

1. Open the Magic Library.mdzip sample project from the <modeling_tool_home>/samples/case studies directory.
2. Click **Tools** > **Report Wizard**. The**Report Wizard** dialog will open. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
3. In the Select Template pane, select **Default Template** > **Web Publisher 2.0**, and click**[IMAGE alt='' src='']**.
4. You can either:
  - select the built-in report data or click [IMAGE alt='' src=''] to create a new one. Type the new report name and description, and then click [IMAGE alt='' src='']. In the Select Report Data pane, you can create a new set of Report Data for the Web Publisher template. The Report Data is a container for a set of custom-defined fields in the template. It can be used to group different report versions.To edit or create a variable in the report data by clicking [IMAGE alt='' src=''], edit or delete information for predefined custom fields or create a new one, and click [IMAGE alt='' src=''].[IMAGE alt='' src='']
5. Click [ATTACHMENT filename='Next_button.png'] .
6. Select the element(s) from the model that you want to include in the report data, and click [ATTACHMENT filename='Add_button.png'] . Select the scope of the report in the open package tree. Select the Model package if you want to have a web-based report of your entire project. [IMAGE alt='' src='']
7. Click [ATTACHMENT filename='Next_button.png'] .
8. Click the[IMAGE alt='' src=''] button to locate the report file location.
9. Select the file location, type the report name, and click [IMAGE alt='' src='']. A generated web report will include a number of folders and files.
10. Select the report image format: **.png*, **.jpg* or**.svg*.
11. Select an option to display empty value information, either **Empty text** or **Custom text**. In some cases, the query may return an empty value that creates blank fields in the report. The **Display empty value as** option is useful when you have a standard representation for blank fields.
12. Select the **[IMAGE alt='' src='']** check box to open the report document with the default editor.
13. After all options have been selected, click [IMAGE alt='' src=''].

To hide or show the Containment menu

- Click the CONTAINMENT menu to hide it, and click it again to show it.

###### [IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
Hiding the Containment Menu.

To expand or collapse the Containment tree

- Click the “ + ” button in the Containment tree to expand it, or click the “ - ” button to collapse it.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The button to expand or collapse the Containment tree.

To reduce or increase the Containment tree width

- Drag the separator line between the containment and the content panel to reduce or increase the width of the Containment tree. The**Web Publisher 2.0**report interface uses ahorizontalscrollbar, which appears when the length of an element's name exceeds the current width of the Containment tree.The default width of the containment tree is**20%**of the**web browser**width.

To show or hide element contents

- Click and re-click the arrow button to show and hide the contents. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Showing and hiding element contents.

To show an element specification, active hyperlink, Submachine of state, or behavior of the Call Behavior action

- Click a diagram's element to show the shorcut menu for opening its specification, Active Hyperlink, Hyperlink, submachine of state, or behavior of the call behavior action. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Web Publisher 2.0 context menu.

To add an Active Hyperlink to a model

You can [add an active hyperlink to any symbol on a diagram](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Defining+hyperlinks). There are three kinds of hyperlinks: Element, File, and URL. However, the Element type hyperlink is available for the Active Hyperlink column on the [Generic Table diagram](https://docs.nomagic.com/display/MD2024xR3/Working+with+Web+Publisher+2.0#WorkingwithWebPublisher2.0-generictable) image only.

#### NOTE: Note

Note

The Web Publisher 2.0 report does not display the Generic Table diagram containing 10,000 elements or more due to the excessive size of the diagram image, making it unable to be rendered and empty.

You can navigate to the target if you double-click the hyperlink**on the diagram in the Web Publisher report. The following figure below shows the Submachine State hyperlink in the Web Publisher report.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The Submachine State hyperlink in the Web Publisher report.

If you double-click the Submachine State in the above example, it navigates to the target and opens it for you as shown in the following figure.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The hyperlink navigates to the target in the Web Publisher report.

Elements in the **Active Hyperlink** column in the **Generic Table** diagram link to the associate elements. If you click an element in this column, you will be navigated to the Specification page of the associated element.

#### NOTE: Note

Note

Only element type is available. File and URL address cannot navigate to the associated artifacts.

generictable

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Elements in the Active Hyperlink column in the Generic Table diagram links to the associated elements in the Specification page.

To display a property ID in the Containment tree

1. Click Tools > Report Wizard > Variable to open the Report Variable dialog.
2. Select the DisplayTreeElementId variable and enter the value true .
3. Click**OK**to show the requirement property IDs in the **Containment** tree. [IMAGE alt='' src='']The requirement property IDs also appear in the **Containment** tree of Web Publisher. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

To go to the index page

- Click the Web Publisher 2.0 at the top-left corner of the screen to go to the index page.

[IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Shortcut to the index page.

To see the description of an element

- On the Specification tab, move your mouse over an element to see the description in a tooltip. [IMAGE alt='' src=''] Showing an element description.

To show property visibility of your report

- In the **Specification** tab, select **Standard**, **Expert**, or **All** from the **Mode** drop-down menu. The mode appears in the property visibility depends upon the mode that you have selected in the modeling tool. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### Property visibility mode types.

To open an Activity, a State Machine, a Collaboration, or an Interaction sub-diagram

- Click an Activity, State Machine, Collaboration, or Interaction diagram to open a sub-diagram associated with an element. [ATTACHMENT filename='Clicking a Diagram Name to Open Its Subdiagrams.png']

###### Clicking a diagram name to open its subdiagrams.

To open the sub-diagrams of a state with Submachine

1. Double-click either a state with a Submachine or a call behavior action of which behavior is specified. For example, double-clicking the last Submachine State *Request Access : Connection* in the following figure.[IMAGE alt='' src=''] 
When you double-click it, the associated diagram opens (see the following figure). [IMAGE alt='' src=''] State machine diagram viewed in web publisher interface.
2. Click the “**+**” button in the Containment tree to expand it, or click the “**-**” button to collapse it. [IMAGE alt='' src='']

###### The button to expand or collapse the Containment tree.

Before generating a report based on the Web Publisher 2.0 template, you can add more variables to it, edit the existing ones, or delete those you do not want to include in your report. </p><p style="text-align: center;"><ac:image><ri:attachment ri:filename="Report Variable Dialog.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Web Publisher 2.0" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;">Report variables of Web Publisher 2.0.</h6><p>The following table shows the variable names and values of the Web Publisher 2.0 template.</p><table class="wrapped"><colgroup><col /><col /></colgroup><tbody><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Value</th></tr><tr><td>Author</td><td>The report's creator.</td></tr><tr><td>Title</td><td>The report's title.</td></tr><tr><td><div class="content-wrapper"><p>HomeImage</p></div></td><td><div class="content-wrapper"><p>Possible values:</p><ul><li>Leave it empty or unspecified to use the MagicDraw icon as the homepage image.</li><li>Enter a diagram name (plain text) to display <span>the selected diagram as the homepage </span><span>image, for example, Software Development Process.</span></li><li><span><span>Enter “mdel://” followed by a model element </span><span>ID to display the element as the homepage image, f</span><span>or example, </span><span>“</span><em><a>mdel://_10_0EAPbeta2_8740266_1126593738250_35764_172</a></em><span>”.</span></span></li><li>Enter the absolute path of an image file on your computer to display the image as the homepage image, for example, <em>file://d://picture//image.jpg</em>.</li><li>Enter the relative path of an image file on your computer to display the image as the homepage image. The relative path starts at the location of the Web Publisher 2.0 template: <em>%APPDATA%\Local\.magicdraw\2021x\data\reports\Web Publisher 2.0\web</em> (<em>%APPDATA%</em> is the location where the user's data are stored, for example, <em>/images/homeimage.jpg</em>).</li><li><p><span><span>Enter the location of an image on the Web to </span><span>display the image as the homepage image, f</span><span>or example, </span><em><a href="http://www.photobucket.com/image.jpg">http://www.photobucket.com/image.jpg</a></em><span>.</span></span></p></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2"><div class="content-wrapper"><p><ac:image ac:align="center"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Diagram as the Homepage Image.png"><ri:page ri:content-title="Working with Web Publisher 2.0" ri:space-key="MD2024xR3" /></ri:attachment></ac:image></p><h6 style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: rgb(112,112,112);">Diagram as the homepage </span>image.</h6></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">UseContextMenu</td><td colspan="1"><p>True: Shows a context menu when right-clicking a diagram element.</p><p>False: Shows an element specification or opens an element, a diagram, or a page specified in any existing active hyperlink when right-clicking a diagram element.</p></td></tr><tr><td>SelectHistoryNode</td><td><p>True: Selects a node when you move backwards or forwards.</p><p>False: T<span>ypes &quot;false&quot; if you want it another way.</span></p></td></tr><tr><td>ExportLinkedFile</td><td><p>True: C<span>opies a linked file from </span><span>a model hyperlink into </span><span>an output report folder.</span></p><p>False: K<span>eeps the link to an absolute path only.</span></p></td></tr><tr><td>ShowAppearsInPage</td><td><p>True: Shows <span>data in a report, and </span><span>opens the <strong>Appears in</strong> tab </span><span>when clicking an element </span><span>in the Containment tree </span><span>or a diagram pane. </span></p><p>False:<span> Hides the Appears in tab </span><span>in a generated report.</span></p></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">ShowAppliedStereotypes</td><td colspan="1"><p>True: Shows applied stereotypes of elements in the Containment tree.</p><p>False: Does not show applied stereotypes of elements in the Containment tree.</p></td></tr><tr><td>AutoNavigateHyperlink</td><td><p>True: <span>Automatically navigates the active </span><span>hyperlink of each element. For </span><span>example, if A has an active </span><span>hyperlink to B and B has an </span><span>active hyperlink to C, then C will </span><span>be shown when you click A.</span></p><p>False: <span>The behavior of navigation to </span><span>active hyperlink is the same as </span><span>that of MagicDraw. For example, </span><span>if A has an active hyperlink to B </span><span>and B has an active hyperlink to </span><span>C, then B will be shown when </span><span>you click A. </span></p></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">DisplayTreeElementId</td><td colspan="1"><p>True: Shows the property ID of an element in the Containment tree.</p><p>False: <span>Types &quot;false&quot; if you want it another way.</span></p></td></tr><tr><td>SVGDiagramResizable</td><td><div class="content-wrapper"><p>True: Resizes SVG images when the browser is minimized.</p><p>False: E<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">nables SVG image </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">linkable capability, </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">but the resizable capability </span><span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">would be disabled.</span></p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="info" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="c77e6fff-8847-4652-8357-e50bc421b15e"><ac:rich-text-body><p>If the &quot;SVGDiagramResizable&quot; is set to True, the SVG image would be resizable on web browser, but it would not be linkable.</p></ac:rich-text-body></ac:structured-macro></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">SkipElementContext</td><td colspan="1"><p>True: Skips the iteration of all elements to create velocity context classified by customized stereotypes, e.g., $CustomizedStereotypeName.</p><p>False: Does not skip the iteration of all elements to create velocity context classified by customized stereotypes.</p></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">GotoLinkByIcon</td><td colspan="1"><p>True: Both the icon and the label of the element in the Containment tree navigate to an active hyperlink.</p><p>False: The icon element navigates to the element's <strong>Specification</strong> tab even if there is an active hyperlink.</p></td></tr><tr><td colspan="1">ExportedImageSize</td><td colspan="1">The percentage (from 10 to 1000) of an exported image size.</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p><p><ac:structured-macro ac:name="anchor" ac:schema-version="1" ac:macro-id="7802b830-21e3-48e0-ab40-c7fbae43d107"><ac:parameter ac:name="">WorkingwithWP</ac:parameter></ac:structured-macro></p><p>The following section contains the instructions on how to work with your Web Publisher report.</p><p><br /></p><p class="auto-cursor-target">To generate a Web Publisher report</p><hr /><ol><li>Open the <em>Magic Library.mdzip</em> sample project from the <em>&lt;modeling_tool_home&gt;/samples/case studies</em> directory.</li><li><p>Click <strong>Tools</strong> &gt; <strong>Report Wizard</strong>.
